## GHSA-7h5p-637f-jfr7 · starcitizenwiki/embedvideo

2026-06-19 · PHP · **HIGH** 8.6 · Pattern: `UNSANITIZED_INPUT→XSS`

### Root cause

The vulnerability existed because user-controlled input, specifically the 'class' parameter, was directly interpolated into an HTML template string without proper sanitization. This allowed an attacker to inject arbitrary HTML and JavaScript code into the rendered page.

### Impact

An attacker could inject malicious scripts into the StarCitizenWiki pages, leading to session hijacking, defacement, or redirection of users to malicious sites.

### Key diff

```
-		return sprintf(
-			$template,
-			$config['class'] ?? '',
+		$templateParser = new TemplateParser( __DIR__ . '/templates' );
+
+		$wrapperContentsHtml = '';
+		if ( ( $config['withConsent'] ?? false ) === true ) {
```

### Fix summary

The patch refactors the HTML generation to use MediaWiki's `TemplateParser` and `Html::element` utility functions. Instead of direct string interpolation, all user-provided values are now passed as template arguments or handled by dedicated HTML escaping functions, preventing the injection of malicious code.

## GHSA-x975-rgx4-5fh4 · appium-mcp

2026-06-19 · JavaScript · **HIGH** 8.2 · Pattern: `UNSANITIZED_INPUT→XSS`

### Root cause

The application was dynamically generating HTML content using user-controlled data (e.g., element.tagName, element.text, element.resourceId, strategy, selector) without proper HTML escaping. This allowed an attacker to inject malicious scripts or HTML into the UI.

### Impact

An attacker could inject arbitrary HTML or JavaScript into the UI, leading to session hijacking, defacement, or redirection to malicious sites if a user views a crafted locator.

### Key diff

```
--- a/src/ui/mcp-ui-utils.ts
+++ b/src/ui/mcp-ui-utils.ts
@@ -720,24 +720,24 @@ export function createLocatorGeneratorUI(
       (element, index) => `
     <div class="locator-card" data-index="${index}">
       <div class="locator-header">
-        <h3>${element.tagName}</h3>
+        <h3>${escapeHtml(element.tagName)}</h3>
         <div class="badges">
           ${element.clickable ? '<span class="badge badge-clickable">Clickable</span>' : ''}
           ${element.enabled ? '<span class="badge badge-enabled">Enabled</span>' : ''}
           ${element.displayed ? '<span class="badge badge-displayed">Displayed</span>' : ''}
         </div>
       </div>
-      ${element.text ? `<p class="element-text"><strong>Text:</strong> ${element.text}</p>` : ''}
-      ${element.contentDesc ? `<p class="element-text"><strong>Content Desc:</strong> ${element.contentDesc}</p>` : ''}
-      ${element.resourceId ? `<p class="element-text"><strong>Resource ID:</strong> <code>${element.resourceId}</code></p>` : ''}
+      ${element.text ? `<p class="element-text"><strong>Text:</strong> ${escapeHtml(element.text)}</p>` : ''}
+      ${element.contentDesc ? `<p class="element-text"><strong>Content Desc:</strong> ${escapeHtml(element.contentDesc)}</p>` : ''}
+      ${element.resourceId ? `<p class="element-text"><strong>Resource ID:</strong> <code>${escapeHtml(element.resourceId)}</code></p>` : ''}
       <div class="locators-list">
         ${Object.entries(element.locators)
           .map(
             ([strategy, selector]) => `
           <div class="locator-item">
-            <span class="strategy">${strategy}</span>
-            <code class="selector">${selector}</code>
-            <button class="test-btn" onclick="testLocator('${strategy}', \`${selector.replace(/`/g, '\`')}\`)">Test</button>
+            <span class="strategy">${escapeHtml(strategy)}</span>
+            <code class="selector">${escapeHtml(selector)}</code>
+            <button class="test-btn" data-strategy="${escapeHtml(strategy)}" data-selector="${escapeHtml(selector)}">Test</button>
           </div>
         `
           )
@@ -1633,3 +1643,12 @@ export function addUIResourceToResponse(
     content: [...response.content, uiResource],
   };
 }
+
+function escapeHtml(value: unknown): string {
+  return String(value)
+    .replace(/&/g, '&amp;')
+    .replace(/</g, '&lt;')
+    .replace(/>/g, '&gt;')
+    .replace(/"/g, '&quot;')
+    .replace(/'/g, '&#039;');
+}
```

### Fix summary

The patch introduces an `escapeHtml` utility function and applies it to all user-controlled data before it is inserted into the HTML template. Additionally, the `onclick` attribute for the 'Test' button was replaced with a safer event listener using `dataset` attributes to prevent potential injection via the `selector`.

## GHSA-4936-9hrh-qqpw · @tinacms/cli

2026-06-19 · JavaScript · **HIGH** 7.8 · Pattern: `UNSANITIZED_INPUT→COMMAND`

### Root cause

The application used a fixed internal marker (`__TINA_INTERNAL__:::`), which was intended to smuggle generated code expressions through JSON.stringify. However, this marker was not sufficiently unique or protected. User-controlled YAML labels, which were processed alongside internally generated markers, could contain this exact string, leading to the user-supplied content being interpreted as executable code during the transformation process.

### Impact

An attacker could inject arbitrary code into the generated TinaCMS configuration files, leading to remote code execution on the system running the migration utility.

### Key diff

```
-"__TINA_INTERNAL__:::(.*?):::"
+const INTERNAL_NONCE = crypto.randomBytes(16).toString('hex');
+const MARKER_OPEN = `__TINA_INTERNAL_${INTERNAL_NONCE}__:::`;
+const MARKER_CLOSE = `:::__TINA_INTERNAL_${INTERNAL_NONCE}__`;
```

### Fix summary

The patch introduces a per-process random nonce into the internal marker, making it unguessable and preventing user-supplied input from forging the marker. Additionally, it adds input validation using `zod` to reject control characters in Forestry names and labels, providing a defense-in-depth measure against unexpected bytes in generated source.

> ⚡ **Pattern match — 50 occurrences**

## GHSA-6v7p-g79w-8964 · msgpack

2026-06-19 · Python · **HIGH** 7.5 · Pattern: `DOS→RESOURCE_EXHAUSTION`

### Root cause

The `msgpack.Unpacker` object's internal state (specifically the `unpack_context`) was not properly cleared or reinitialized after an error occurred during unpacking. This led to a corrupted state where subsequent reuse of the Unpacker could result in an out-of-bounds read when accessing the internal stack, causing a crash.

### Impact

An attacker could provide malformed MessagePack data that, when processed by a vulnerable `Unpacker` instance and then followed by valid data, would cause the application to crash due to an out-of-bounds read. This leads to a denial of service.

### Key diff

```
--- a/msgpack/_unpacker.pyx
+++ b/msgpack/_unpacker.pyx
@@ -483,7 +485,9 @@ cdef class Unpacker:
                 else:
                     raise OutOfData("No more data to unpack.")
-            elif ret == -2:
+
+            unpack_clear(&self.ctx)
+            if ret == -2:
                 raise FormatError
             elif ret == -3:
                 raise StackError
```

### Fix summary

The patch ensures that the `unpack_context` is properly cleared and reinitialized after an error occurs during `unpack_execute` (both for `unpack_construct` and `unpack_skip`). Additionally, `unpack_clear` was modified to call `unpack_init` to fully reset the context, and a `map_key` reference is explicitly cleared after use to prevent potential leaks.

## GHSA-c29q-5xm7-5p62 · starcitizenwiki/embedvideo

2026-06-19 · PHP · **HIGH** 7.5 · Pattern: `UNSANITIZED_INPUT→XSS`

### Root cause

The vulnerability existed because exception messages, which could contain unsanitized user-controlled input (specifically the service name), were directly rendered as HTML in error boxes without proper escaping. This allowed an attacker to inject arbitrary HTML and script code into the page.

### Impact

An attacker could inject malicious scripts into the wiki page, leading to stored Cross-Site Scripting (XSS). This could allow them to steal user cookies, deface the website, or perform actions on behalf of other users.

### Key diff

```
--- a/includes/EmbedVideo.php
+++ b/includes/EmbedVideo.php
@@ -172,11 +171,11 @@ public static function parseEVL( Parser $parser, PPFrame $frame, array $args ):
 			$ev->addModules();
 
 			if ( empty( $ev->args['text'] ) ) {
-				throw new InvalidArgumentException( $ev->error( 'missingparams', $ev->args['service'] )[0] );
+				throw EmbedVideoException::newWithHtml( $ev->errorBoxHtml( 'missingparams', $ev->args['service'] ) );
 			}
-		} catch ( InvalidArgumentException $e ) {
+		} catch ( EmbedVideoException $e ) {
 			return [
-				$e->getMessage(),
+				$e->getHtml(),
```

### Fix summary

The patch introduces a custom `EmbedVideoException` class and modifies error handling to ensure that error messages are properly HTML-escaped before being rendered. Instead of directly returning raw exception messages, the code now uses `Html::element` to construct the error box, ensuring that all content is escaped.

## GHSA-hp36-v28f-w3r4 · flat-to-nested

2026-06-19 · JavaScript · **HIGH** 7.5 · Pattern: `PROTOTYPE_POLLUTION→OVERRIDE`

### Root cause

The vulnerability existed because the `flat-to-nested` library used plain JavaScript objects (`{}`) as hash maps for `temp` and `pendingChildOf`. When processing input records, if an attacker supplied a `parent` or `id` key with a value like `__proto__`, it would allow them to access and modify the `Object.prototype` through `temp[parent]` or `pendingChildOf[id]`, leading to prototype pollution.

### Impact

An attacker could inject or modify properties on `Object.prototype`, which could affect all objects in the application. This could lead to denial of service, remote code execution in certain contexts, or other unexpected behavior depending on how the application uses object properties.

### Key diff

```
--- a/index.js
+++ b/index.js
-    temp = {};
-    pendingChildOf = {};
+    temp = Object.create(null);
+    pendingChildOf = Object.create(null);
```

### Fix summary

The patch mitigates the vulnerability by changing the initialization of `temp` and `pendingChildOf` from plain objects (`{}`) to `Object.create(null)`. This creates objects without a prototype chain, preventing keys like `__proto__` from referencing `Object.prototype` and thus stopping prototype pollution.

> ⚡ **Pattern match — 15 occurrences**
> Languages: JavaScript
> → GHSA-fw9q-39r9-c252
> → GHSA-rv5g-f82m-qrvv
> → GHSA-mhwj-73qx-jqxm

> → GHSA-m2hg-wjq3-28wq
> → GHSA-cmxg-94mg-jq94
> → GHSA-c4cf-2hgv-2qv6
> → GHSA-q3fm-4wcw-g57x
> → GHSA-9m6g-wc8r-q59c
> → GHSA-2933-q333-qg83
> → GHSA-f49m-vf83-692w

> → GHSA-c96f-x56v-gq3h

## GHSA-6mwx-4547-5vc9 · github.com/openbao/openbao

2026-06-19 · Go · **MODERATE** 6.8 · Pattern: `UNSANITIZED_INPUT→LDAP`

### Root cause

The application incorrectly used `ldaputil.EscapeLDAPValue` instead of `ldap.EscapeFilter` when constructing LDAP filters. `EscapeLDAPValue` is designed for escaping values within an LDAP attribute, not for escaping user-controlled input within an LDAP search filter, leading to a bypass of the intended sanitization.

### Impact

An attacker could inject arbitrary LDAP filter syntax into search queries, potentially leading to unauthorized access, information disclosure, or manipulation of LDAP entries by bypassing authentication or authorization checks.

### Key diff

```
- bindUser := fmt.Sprintf("%s@%s", ldaputil.EscapeLDAPValue(dn), conf.UPNDomain)
+ bindUser := fmt.Sprintf("%s@%s", ldap.EscapeFilter(dn), conf.UPNDomain)

- filter := fmt.Sprintf("(userPrincipalName=%s@%s)", EscapeLDAPValue(username), cfg.UPNDomain)
+ filter := fmt.Sprintf("(userPrincipalName=%s@%s)", ldap.EscapeFilter(username), cfg.UPNDomain)
```

### Fix summary

The patch replaces the incorrect `ldaputil.EscapeLDAPValue` function with the correct `ldap.EscapeFilter` function from the `go-ldap/ldap/v3` library. This ensures that user-provided input is properly escaped when constructing LDAP search filters, preventing injection attacks.

> ⚡ **Pattern match — 3 occurrences**
> Languages: Go, Java
> → GHSA-5835-4gvc-32pc
> → GHSA-c3fc-8qff-9hwx

🔗 [View commit](https://github.com/openbao/openbao/commit/10b7825c714c1ef25b6c3c1c2cd6ecd8747c0659)

## GHSA-3j69-69wj-xqx2 · ujson

2026-06-19 · Python · **MODERATE** 6.5 · Pattern: `UNCLASSIFIED`

### Root cause

The UltraJSON library's `ujson.dumps()` function did not strictly validate UTF-8 sequences, allowing malformed or truncated UTF-8 input to be silently rewritten into valid, but potentially different, UTF-8. This could lead to data corruption or inconsistencies between systems that handle JSON.

### Impact

An attacker could provide specially crafted malformed UTF-8 strings that, when processed by `ujson.dumps()`, would be silently altered. This could lead to data integrity issues, bypass of input validation in downstream systems, or potentially cause unexpected behavior in applications relying on the exact byte representation of strings.

### Key diff

```
--- a/src/ujson/lib/ultrajsonenc.c
+++ b/src/ujson/lib/ultrajsonenc.c
@@ -347,17 +347,24 @@ static int Buffer_EscapeStringValidated (JSOBJ obj, JSONObjectEncoder *enc, cons
         continue;
       }
 
+      // https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/UTF-8#Description
       case 2:
       {
         JSUTF32 in;
         JSUTF16 in16;
 
-        if (end - io < 1)
+        if (end - io < 2)
         {
           enc->offset += (of - enc->offset);
           SetError (obj, enc, "Unterminated UTF-8 sequence when encoding string");
           return FALSE;
         }
+        if ((io[1] & 0xc0) != 0x80)
+        {
+          enc->offset += (of - enc->offset);
+          SetError (obj, enc, "Invalid continuation byte in 2-byte UTF-8 sequence detected when encoding string");
+          return FALSE;
+        }
```

### Fix summary

The patch introduces stricter validation for UTF-8 sequences during string encoding and decoding. It adds checks for correct continuation bytes, minimum length requirements for multi-byte sequences, and prevents encoding of characters outside the valid Unicode range (U+10FFFF). Error messages are now returned for invalid or overlong sequences instead of silent rewriting.

## GHSA-8w8f-r2xv-4q4j · github.com/openbao/openbao

2026-06-19 · Go · **MODERATE** 6.5 · Pattern: `DOS→RESOURCE_EXHAUSTION`

### Root cause

The vulnerability stemmed from an incorrect locking mechanism within the transit secrets engine. When creating a key with `derived: true` for asymmetric key types, the system attempted to acquire a read lock on a key that had not yet been fully initialized or was in an inconsistent state. This led to a deadlock or a panic, causing the service to crash.

### Impact

An attacker could trigger a denial of service by sending a specially crafted request to create a transit key, leading to the OpenBao service crashing and becoming unavailable.

### Key diff

```
--- a/builtin/logical/transit/path_hmac.go
+++ b/builtin/logical/transit/path_hmac.go
@@ -135,9 +135,6 @@ func (b *backend) pathHMACWrite(ctx context.Context, req *logical.Request, d *fr
 	if p == nil {
 		return logical.ErrorResponse("encryption key not found"), logical.ErrInvalidRequest
 	}
-	if !b.System().CachingDisabled() {
-		p.Lock(false)
-	}
 	defer p.Unlock()
```

### Fix summary

The patch removes unnecessary `Lock(false)` calls (read locks) in several transit key-related paths and introduces `GetPolicyExclusive` to ensure an exclusive write lock is acquired when necessary, particularly during key creation and modification. This prevents deadlocks and ensures proper synchronization during key operations.

## GHSA-jvcm-f35g-w78p · network-ai

2026-06-19 · JavaScript · **MODERATE** 6.5 · Pattern: `PATH_TRAVERSAL→FILE_READ`

### Root cause

The original code for sandbox path-prefix checks did not properly anchor the blocked path prefixes, allowing an attacker to bypass the checks by appending a path separator. For example, if '/foo' was blocked, an attacker could still access '/foo/../bar' if the check only looked for 'startsWith('/foo')' without ensuring a path separator followed.

### Impact

An attacker could bypass sandbox restrictions to access or manipulate files outside the intended base directory, potentially leading to information disclosure, unauthorized file modification, or even remote code execution within the sandboxed environment.

### Key diff

```
--- a/lib/agent-runtime.ts
+++ b/lib/agent-runtime.ts
@@ -395,7 +395,7 @@ export class SandboxPolicy {
     const normalized = this.resolvePath(filePath);
     if (!normalized) return false;
 
-    // Check blocked paths
+    // Check blocked paths (sep-anchored prefix — GHSA-jvcm-f35g-w78p)
     for (const blocked of this.config.blockedPaths) {
       const blockedAbs = resolve(this.config.basePath
```

### Fix summary

The patch modifies the path-prefix checks to ensure that blocked paths are anchored with a path separator. This prevents bypasses where a blocked prefix like '/foo' could be circumvented by accessing '/foo/../bar'. Additionally, it introduces checks for path traversal characters in backup IDs and uses `lstatSync` to avoid following symlinks, further hardening file operations.

## GHSA-48x2-6pr9-2jjf · network-ai

2026-06-19 · JavaScript · **MODERATE** 6.1 · Pattern: `PATH_TRAVERSAL→FILE_WRITE`

### Root cause

The `EnvironmentManager.restore()` method constructed a backup path by directly joining a user-controlled `backupId` with a base directory. This allowed an attacker to use path traversal sequences (e.g., `../`) in the `backupId` to specify an arbitrary directory outside the intended backup location.

### Impact

An attacker could copy arbitrary directories from the server's file system into an environment's data directory, potentially leading to information disclosure or overwriting critical files if the application later processes these copied files.

### Key diff

```
--- a/lib/env-manager.ts
+++ b/lib/env-manager.ts
@@ -474,7 +475,15 @@ export class EnvironmentManager {
   restore(env: EnvName, backupId: string): RestoreResult {
     const envDir = this.getDataDir(env);
     const backupsDir = join(envDir, '.backups');
-    const backupPath = join(backupsDir, backupId);
+    // Reject IDs with path separators, dots, or other traversal characters (GHSA-48x2-6pr9-2jjf)
+    if (!/^[\w\-]+$/.test(backupId)) {
+      throw new Error(`Invalid backup ID: '${backupId}'`);
+    }
+    const backupPath = resolve(join(backupsDir, backupId));
+    if (dirname(backupPath) !== resolve(backupsDir)) {
+      throw new Error(`Backup ID '${backupId}' would escape the backups directory`);
+    }
 
     if (!existsSync(backupPath)) {
       throw new Error(`Backup '${backupId}' not found for environment '${env}'`);
```

### Fix summary

The patch introduces validation for the `backupId` in `EnvironmentManager.restore()`, ensuring it only contains alphanumeric characters and hyphens, and explicitly checks that the resolved path does not escape the intended backup directory. Similar path validation and resolution are applied to `rmSync` calls in `pruneBackups` to prevent arbitrary file deletion.

## GHSA-4cc2-g9w2-fhf6 · zeep

2026-06-19 · Python · **MODERATE** 5.9 · Pattern: `SSRF→INTERNAL_ACCESS`

### Root cause

The Zeep library, when parsing WSDL or XSD documents, would by default allow transitive fetches of external resources (e.g., via `xsd:import`, `xsd:include`, `wsdl:import`) from arbitrary HTTP/HTTPS URLs. This meant that if an attacker could supply a malicious WSDL/XSD, they could force the server to make requests to internal network resources or other external services.

### Impact

An attacker could leverage this vulnerability to perform Server-Side Request Forgery (SSRF), potentially accessing internal network resources, cloud metadata endpoints, or other services that the vulnerable application has network access to.

### Key diff

```
--- a/src/zeep/loader.py
+++ b/src/zeep/loader.py
@@ -18,6 +18,8 @@
 
     def resolve(self, url, pubid, context):
         if urlparse(url).scheme in ("http", "https"):
+            if self.settings.forbid_external:
+                raise ExternalReferenceForbidden(url)
             content = self.transport.load(url)
             return self.resolve_string(content, context)
```

### Fix summary

The patch introduces a new `forbid_external` setting, which defaults to `False` for backward compatibility but can be enabled to prevent transitive external HTTP/HTTPS requests during WSDL/XSD parsing. It also modifies the `ImportResolver` and `load_external` functions to check this setting and raise an `ExternalReferenceForbidden` exception if a forbidden external reference is attempted. The initial user-supplied document is still loaded, but subsequent imports are blocked.

## GHSA-mxjx-28vx-xjjj · network-ai

2026-06-19 · JavaScript · **MODERATE** 5.9 · Pattern: `MISSING_AUTH→ENDPOINT`

### Root cause

The ApprovalInbox HTTP server, which handles agent action approvals, did not implement any authentication mechanism for its POST /approve and POST /deny endpoints. This allowed any process capable of reaching the HTTP server to approve or deny pending agent actions without authorization.

### Impact

An attacker could approve or deny any pending agent action, potentially leading to unauthorized execution of commands or manipulation of the agent's behavior, compromising the integrity and security of the system.

### Key diff

```
--- a/lib/approval-inbox.ts
+++ b/lib/approval-inbox.ts
@@ -389,12 +398,14 @@ export class ApprovalInbox extends EventEmitter {
     // POST /:id/approve
     const approveMatch = subPath.match(/^/([a-f0-9]+)/approve$/);
     if (approveMatch && req.method === 'POST') {
+      if (!this.checkAuth(req, res)) return;
       this.readBody(req).then((body) => {
         const approvedBy = typeof body.approvedBy === 'string' ? body.approvedBy : 'anonymous';
         const reason = typeof body.reason === 'string' ? body.reason : undefined;
         this.approve(id, { approvedBy, reason });
       });
     }
     // POST /:id/deny
     const denyMatch = subPath.match(/^/([a-f0-9]+)/deny$/);
     if (denyMatch && req.method === 'POST') {
+      if (!this.checkAuth(req, res)) return;
       this.readBody(req).then((body) => {
         const deniedBy = typeof body.deniedBy === 'string' ? body.deniedBy : undefined;
```

### Fix summary

The patch introduces an optional 'secret' bearer token for the ApprovalInbox. When configured, all POST requests to /approve and /deny endpoints now require a valid 'Authorization: Bearer <secret>' header. A `timingSafeEqual` comparison is used to prevent timing attacks, and requests without a valid token are rejected with 401 or 403 status codes.

## GHSA-6x2m-p4xp-wg22 · network-ai

2026-06-19 · JavaScript · **MODERATE** 5.5 · Pattern: `PATH_TRAVERSAL→FILE_READ`

### Root cause

The `EnvironmentManager.backup()` function used `statSync` instead of `lstatSync` when traversing directories for backup. This caused it to follow symbolic links, allowing an attacker to create a symlink pointing outside the environment root and include arbitrary files from the filesystem in the backup.

### Impact

An attacker could craft a symbolic link within their environment to point to sensitive files or directories outside the environment's root. When a backup is performed, these external files would be included in the backup, leading to information disclosure.

### Key diff

```
--- a/lib/env-manager.ts
+++ b/lib/env-manager.ts
@@ -603,10 +619,11 @@ export class EnvironmentManager {
         const full = join(current, entry);
         const rel = prefix ? `${prefix}/${entry}` : entry;
         try {
-          const info = statSync(full);
+          const info = lstatSync(full); // lstat: never follow symlinks out of backup root (GHSA-6x2m-p4xp-wg22)
+          if (info.isSymbolicLink()) continue; // skip symlinks entirely
           if (info.isDirectory()) {
             walk(full, rel);
-          } else {
+          } else if (info.isFile()) {
             results.push(rel);
           }
         } catch { /* skip */ }
```

### Fix summary

The patch changes `statSync` to `lstatSync` in the backup process to prevent following symbolic links. It also explicitly skips symbolic links and only backs up regular files. Additionally, it adds validation to `backupId` in `restore` and `pruneBackups` to prevent path traversal when restoring or deleting backups.

## GHSA-wwf9-7jrc-rv4q · @outerbase/studio

2026-06-19 · JavaScript · **MODERATE** 4.4 · Pattern: `UNSANITIZED_INPUT→XSS`

### Root cause

The application was directly rendering user-supplied text content (markdown) into the DOM using `dangerouslySetInnerHTML` after performing some basic string replacements for markdown formatting. This allowed an attacker to inject arbitrary HTML and script tags, as the replacements were insufficient to sanitize malicious input.

### Impact

An attacker could inject malicious scripts into the text widget, which would execute in the context of other users viewing the widget. This could lead to session hijacking, authentication token exposure, or defacement of the application.

### Key diff

```
-        <span
-          dangerouslySetInnerHTML={{
-            __html: markdown,
-          }}
-        ></span>
+        <span>{markdown}</span>
```

### Fix summary

The patch removes the custom markdown parsing and the use of `dangerouslySetInnerHTML`. Instead, the user-supplied text is now rendered directly as plain text within a `<span>` element, preventing any HTML or script injection.

## GHSA-78vr-q6cf-c7p6 · craftcms/commerce

2026-06-19 · PHP · **MODERATE** 0.0 · Pattern: `INTEGER_OVERFLOW→BOUNDARY`

### Root cause

The `setPaymentAmount` method in the `Order` class lacked validation to ensure that the payment amount was a non-negative value. This allowed an attacker to set a negative payment amount, which could lead to an incorrect order balance.

### Impact

An attacker could manipulate the payment amount to a negative value, potentially causing an order to appear fully paid or overpaid when it was not, leading to financial discrepancies or free products/services.

### Key diff

```
--- a/src/elements/Order.php
+++ b/src/elements/Order.php
@@ -2456,7 +2458,10 @@ public function setPaymentAmount(float $amount): void
     {
         $paymentCurrency = Plugin::getInstance()->getPaymentCurrencies()->getPaymentCurrencyByIso($this->getPaymentCurrency());
         $amount = Currency::round($amount, $paymentCurrency);
-        $this->_paymentAmount = $amount;
+        if($amount >= 0) {
+            $this->_paymentAmount = $amount;
+        }
     }
```

### Fix summary

The patch adds a conditional check in the `setPaymentAmount` method to ensure that the `$amount` is greater than or equal to zero before assigning it to the `_paymentAmount` property. If the amount is negative, the property will remain null, preventing the invalid state.

> ⚡ **Pattern match — 12 occurrences**
> Languages: Go, C#, RUST, PHP, Python
> → GHSA-r4fg-73rc-hhh7
> → GHSA-26qp-ffjh-2x4v
> → GHSA-v67w-737x-v2c9
> → GHSA-6973-8887-87ff
> → GHSA-38c5-483c-4qqp
> → GHSA-5r97-79vw-qvm4
> → GHSA-c55g-rp4x-fx84
> → GHSA-7gcf-g7xr-8hxj
> → GHSA-8wr5-jm2h-8r4f
> → GHSA-6r8x-57c9-28j4
> → GHSA-xj96-63gp-2gmr

🔗 [View commit](https://github.com/craftcms/commerce/commit/9a88392b3074aa132a9455d4f4b582411df52c74)

## GHSA-c7jm-38gq-h67h · org.http4k:http4k-security-digest

2026-06-19 · Java · **MODERATE** 0.0 · Pattern: `INSECURE_DEFAULT→CONFIG`

### Root cause

The `DigestAuthProvider` and `ServerFilters.DigestAuth` in http4k defaulted the `nonceVerifier` to an always-true lambda. This effectively disabled the replay protection mechanism inherent in Digest Authentication, as any nonce provided by an attacker would be considered valid.

### Impact

An attacker could intercept valid Digest Authentication credentials and replay them to gain unauthorized access to protected resources, bypassing the intended security measure against such attacks.

### Key diff

```
--- a/core/security/digest/src/main/kotlin/org/http4k/security/digest/DigestAuthProvider.kt
+++ b/core/security/digest/src/main/kotlin/org/http4k/security/digest/DigestAuthProvider.kt
@@ -26,7 +26,7 @@ class DigestAuthProvider(
     private val qop: List<Qop>,
     private val algorithm: String,
     private val nonceGenerator: NonceGenerator,
-    private val nonceVerifier: NonceVerifier = { true },
+    private val nonceVerifier: NonceVerifier,
     private val digestMode: DigestMode = DigestMode.Standard
 ) {
 
--- a/core/security/digest/src/main/kotlin/org/http4k/filter/serverFilterExtensions.kt
+++ b/core/security/digest/src/main/kotlin/org/http4k/filter/serverFilterExtensions.kt
@@ -13,7 +13,7 @@ fun ServerFilters.DigestAuth(
     qop: List<Qop> = listOf(Auth),
     digestMode: DigestMode = Standard,
     nonceGenerator: NonceGenerator,
-    nonceVerifier: NonceVerifier = { true },
+    nonceVerifier: NonceVerifier,
     algorithm: String = "MD5",
     usernameKey: RequestLens<String>? = null,
 ): Filter {
```

### Fix summary

The patch removes the default `nonceVerifier = { true }` from both `DigestAuthProvider` and `ServerFilters.DigestAuth`. This change makes the `nonceVerifier` a mandatory parameter, forcing developers to explicitly provide a proper nonce verification mechanism, thus re-enabling replay protection.

## GHSA-h5gm-x9wr-vhcm · craftcms/commerce

2026-06-19 · PHP · **MODERATE** 0.0 · Pattern: `DOS→RESOURCE_EXHAUSTION`

### Root cause

The existing rate limiting mechanism for cart actions only applied when a 'number' parameter (cart number) was explicitly passed. It did not consider other parameters like 'couponCode', allowing an attacker to bypass the rate limit by attempting to apply coupon codes without specifying a cart number.

### Impact

An attacker could perform an unlimited number of attempts to guess valid coupon codes through brute-force, potentially discovering active coupons and using them for unauthorized discounts.

### Key diff

```
--- a/src/controllers/CartController.php
+++ b/src/controllers/CartController.php
@@ -88,14 +93,16 @@ public function behaviors(): array
                 'only' => ['get-cart', 'update-cart', 'load-cart', 'complete'],
                 'enableRateLimitHeaders' => false,
                 'user' => function() {
-                    // Only apply rate limiting when a cart number is explicitly passed
-                    $isActive = Craft::$app->getRequest()->getBodyParam('number') || Craft::$app->getRequest()->getQueryParam('number');
+                    // Only apply rate limiting when a cart number or coupon code is explicitly passed
+                    $request = Craft::$app->getRequest();
+                    $isActive = collect(self::RATE_LIMITED_PARAMS)
+                        ->contains(fn($param) => $request->getBodyParam($param) || $request->getQueryParam($param));
 
                     return $isActive ? new IpRateLimitIdentity([
                         'limit' => 1,
                         'window' => 1,
-                        'keyPrefix' => 'cart-number-rate-limit',
-                        'ip' => Craft::$app->getRequest()->getUserIP() ?? 'unknown',
+                        'keyPrefix' => 'cart-rate-limit',
+                        'ip' => $request->getUserIP() ?? 'unknown',
                     ]) : null;
                 },
```

### Fix summary

The patch extends the rate limiting logic to apply when either a 'number' or 'couponCode' parameter is present in the request. It introduces a constant `RATE_LIMITED_PARAMS` to define which parameters trigger the rate limit and updates the rate limit identity key prefix for broader applicability.

## GHSA-jrpc-7vxp-69p6 · org.http4k:http4k-core

2026-06-19 · Java · **MODERATE** 0.0 · Pattern: `INSECURE_DEFAULT→CONFIG`

### Root cause

The reverse proxy's default host matching logic used a 'contains' substring comparison instead of an exact match for the 'Host' header. This allowed an attacker to craft a 'Host' header that contained a legitimate host name but also included a malicious subdomain, leading to traffic being misrouted.

### Impact

An attacker could potentially bypass security controls, access internal services, or redirect traffic to an unintended backend by manipulating the Host header to match a substring of a legitimate target.

### Key diff

```
--- a/core/core/src/main/kotlin/org/http4k/routing/ReverseProxy.kt
+++ b/core/core/src/main/kotlin/org/http4k/routing/ReverseProxy.kt
@@ -2,28 +2,49 @@ package org.http4k.routing
 
 import org.http4k.core.HttpHandler
 import org.http4k.core.Request
+import org.http4k.routing.ReverseProxyHostMatcher.Companion.Contains
 
 /**
  * Simple Reverse Proxy which will split and direct traffic to the appropriate
- * HttpHandler based on the content of the Host header
+ * HttpHandler based on the content of the Host header.
+ *
+ * Optionally takes a [ReverseProxyHostMatcher] to determine how the host header is matched: defaults to A.contains(B)
  */
-fun reverseProxy(vararg hostToHandler: Pair<String, HttpHandler>): HttpHandler =
-    reverseProxyRouting(*hostToHandler)
+fun reverseProxy(
+    vararg hostToHandler: Pair<String, HttpHandler>, matcher: ReverseProxyHostMatcher = Contains
+): HttpHandler =
+    reverseProxyRouting(*hostToHandler, matcher = matcher)
```

### Fix summary

The patch introduces a `ReverseProxyHostMatcher` interface and changes the default matching behavior from `Contains` (substring) to `Exact` for the `Host` header. This ensures that the host header must precisely match the configured host for routing to occur.

## GHSA-mwqm-4fw3-cjvr · symfony/ux-autocomplete

2026-06-19 · PHP · **MODERATE** 0.0 · Pattern: `UNSANITIZED_INPUT→XSS`

### Root cause

The vulnerability existed because the autocomplete component was rendering AJAX response data directly into the HTML without proper escaping. Specifically, the `item[labelField]` value, which could contain user-controlled input, was inserted into `<div>` elements in the `option` and `item` render functions without being sanitized.

### Impact

An attacker could inject malicious scripts or HTML into the autocomplete suggestions, leading to Cross-Site Scripting (XSS) attacks. This could allow them to steal user cookies, deface the application, or perform actions on behalf of the victim.

### Key diff

```
-                option: (item: any) => `<div>${item[labelField]}</div>`,
-                item: (item: any) => `<div>${item[labelField]}</div>`,
+                option: (item: any, escape: typeof escape_html) =>
+                    `<div>${this.optionsAsHtmlValue ? item[labelField] : escape(item[labelField])}</div>`,
+                item: (item: any, escape: typeof escape_html) =>
+                    `<div>${this.optionsAsHtmlValue ? item[labelField] : escape(item[labelField])}</div>`,
```

### Fix summary

The patch introduces an `escape` function to sanitize the `item[labelField]` value before rendering it in the `option` and `item` templates. It conditionally applies this escaping based on a new `optionsAsHtmlValue` property, ensuring that by default, user-provided data is safely escaped. Additionally, a normalizer that would automatically disable `options_as_html` when `autocomplete_url` was present was removed, simplifying the logic.

> ⚡ **Pattern match — 73 occurrences**
> Languages: Python, JavaScript, PHP, Java, Go, RUST, Ruby
> → GHSA-8wrq-fv5f-pfp2
> → GHSA-95h2-gj7x-gx9w
> → GHSA-rqp3-gf5h-mrqx
> → GHSA-cpm7-cfpx-3hvp
> → GHSA-fh64-r2vc-xvhr
> → GHSA-r758-8hxw-4845
> → GHSA-9pr4-rf97-79qh
> → GHSA-vffh-x6r8-xx99
> → GHSA-gph2-j4c9-vhhr
> → GHSA-855c-r2vq-c292

## GHSA-pr33-38xx-6r26 · org.http4k:http4k-core

2026-06-19 · Java · **MODERATE** 0.0 · Pattern: `INFO_DISCLOSURE→ERROR_MESSAGE`

### Root cause

The previous `BasicCookieStorage` implementation did not enforce RFC 6265 cookie scoping rules. It stored all cookies in a global jar and sent them with every outgoing request, regardless of the cookie's domain, path, or secure flag. This meant cookies intended for one origin could be leaked to another.

### Impact

An attacker could potentially gain access to sensitive cookies (e.g., session tokens, authentication credentials) if the client interacted with multiple hosts, leading to cross-origin credential leakage and potential session hijacking or unauthorized access.

### Key diff

```
--- a/core/core/src/main/kotlin/org/http4k/filter/cookie/clientCookies.kt
+++ b/core/core/src/main/kotlin/org/http4k/filter/cookie/clientCookies.kt
-class BasicCookieStorage : CookieStorage {
-    private val storage = ConcurrentHashMap<String, LocalCookie>()
-
-    override fun store(cookies: List<LocalCookie>) = cookies.forEach { storage[it.cookie.name] = it }
-
-    override fun retrieve(): List<LocalCookie> = storage.values.toList()
-
-    override fun remove(name: String) {
-        storage.remove(name)
-    }
+}
+class DefaultCookieStorage : CookieStorage {
```

### Fix summary

The `BasicCookieStorage` was deprecated and renamed to `InsecureCookieStorage`. A new `DefaultCookieStorage` was introduced, which correctly implements RFC 6265 cookie scoping, enforcing domain, path, and secure flag restrictions. The `ClientFilters.Cookies` now defaults to using `DefaultCookieStorage`.

> ⚡ **Pattern match — 25 occurrences**
> Languages: RUST, PHP, Java, JavaScript, Go, Python, Ruby
> → GHSA-hfpq-x728-986j
> → GHSA-3vxg-x5f8-f5qf
> → GHSA-27h3-crw2-q36w
> → GHSA-c276-fj82-f2pq
> → GHSA-hppc-g8h3-xhp3
> → GHSA-xr49-f4rh-qcjf
> → GHSA-qxrw-f6fh-34r7
> → GHSA-fmxf-pm6p-7xgm
> → GHSA-jxx9-px88-pj69
> → GHSA-58qx-3vcg-4xpx
> → GHSA-vhjm-w67q-g75c
> → GHSA-j5f8-grm9-p9fc
> → GHSA-6vgg-xhvh-38ff
> → GHSA-qxh6-94w6-9r5p
> → GHSA-hpj7-wq8m-9hgp
> → GHSA-hgg8-fqqc-vfmw
> → GHSA-396q-4vc8-28x9
> → GHSA-xqr9-4wvv-gvch
> → GHSA-p7h3-7q52-72w8
> → GHSA-588f-fvcv-xhvf
> → GHSA-q6gh-6v2r-hjv3

## GHSA-vmhf-c436-hxj4 · jupyterlab

2026-06-19 · Python · **MODERATE** 0.0 · Pattern: `UNSANITIZED_INPUT→XSS`

### Root cause

The JupyterLab extension manager displayed package metadata, including the 'homepage_url', without proper sanitization or validation of the URI protocol. An attacker could inject arbitrary JavaScript by crafting a malicious 'homepage_url' with a 'javascript:' protocol.

### Impact

An attacker could execute arbitrary JavaScript in the context of the user's browser when they view the malicious extension's details in the extension manager, potentially leading to session hijacking, data theft, or further client-side attacks.

### Key diff

```
--- a/packages/extensionmanager/src/widget.tsx
+++ b/packages/extensionmanager/src/widget.tsx
@@ -75,7 +85,7 @@ function ListEntry(props: ListEntry.IProperties): React.ReactElement<any> {

         <div className="jp-extensionmanager-entry-title">
           <div className="jp-extensionmanager-entry-name">

+            {entry.homepage_url && isProtocolAllowed(entry.homepage_url) ? (
               <a

```

### Fix summary

The patch introduces a new function, `isProtocolAllowed`, which explicitly checks if a URL's protocol is either 'http:' or 'https:'. This function is then used to validate the `entry.homepage_url` before it is rendered as an anchor tag's `href` attribute, preventing the use of malicious protocols like 'javascript:'.
